The paper establishes that, under a Gaussian channel model with random node placement and multicast sessions, each session can achieve a capacity of at least \( c_8 \sqrt{n} / (n_s \sqrt{k}) \) with high probability, given constraints on \( k \) and \( n_s \). This result generalizes prior unicast findings and is presented in conference C.2.

The paper proposes crash recovery protocols for shared memory database systems on cache-coherent multiprocessors, focusing on transaction aborts, rollback correctness, and minimal overhead, within the context of database systems (H.2).
The paper introduces **LyriC**, an object-oriented query language for databases handling spatial, temporal, and constraint data, unifying constraint-based design, optimization, and spatial databases by extending XSQL with path expressions and first-class constraint objects. Relevant conference: H.2 (Database Management).
The paper introduces the monoid calculus as an effective database calculus for object-oriented query languages like OQL, demonstrating its ability to handle diverse collection types, aggregations, nested queries, and extensions for vectors, arrays, identity, and updates. Relevant conference: H.2 (Database Management).
The paper presents an efficient branch-and-bound R-tree traversal algorithm for k nearest neighbors, evaluates search strategies and pruning metrics, and demonstrates performance through experiments. Relevant conference: H.2.
The paper presents a method for predictable worst-case performance in multi-dimensional index structures, preserving B-tree-like logarithmic access times and minimum node occupancy via controlled recursive partitioning, relevant to the conference topic 'H.3'.
The paper analyzes how Minimum Bounding Rectangles (MBRs) convey topological relations in spatial databases, applies these findings to optimize query performance in R-trees and their variants, and explores handling complex spatial queries, with relevance to the H.2 database systems conference.
The paper introduces and compares the *sorted neighborhood* and *clustering-based* methods for efficiently and accurately merging data from multiple databases (the *merge/purge* problem), proposing a *multi-pass* approach with Transitive Closure to enhance accuracy. Relevant conference: H.2.
The paper introduces *indexing by class-division (CD)*, an efficient extension of the class hierarchy index (CH) technique for OODBs that improves range query performance while maintaining practical implementation using B+-trees, albeit with modest space and update overhead. It is related to the conference category H.3.
The paper proposes an efficient indexing technique using Hidden Markov Models (HMMs) and a modified trie structure for fast retrieval of handwritten text in large ink databases, with implementations for both main-memory and disk-based systems, relevant to the H.3 conference.
The paper proposes a fast, linear-time algorithm for k-dimensional mapping of objects while preserving dissimilarities, enabling efficient retrieval and visualization, outperforming traditional MDS in speed and scalability. It is related to conference topic H.3.
The paper proposes a hash-based algorithm for efficient 2-itemset generation in large transaction databases, improving performance by reducing computational costs. Relevant to conference topic: H.2 (Database Management).
The paper compares four crash recovery techniques in an OODBMS (page differencing, sub-page differencing, whole-page logging, and redo-at-server) using the OO7 benchmark and finds that differencing-based methods outperform whole-page logging. Relevant conference: H.2.
The paper, presented at conference H.2, concludes that the most effective histograms for database query optimization balance accuracy and efficiency by precisely tracking frequencies of a few attribute values while assuming uniformity for the rest, with optimality determined by self-join queries.
The paper examines efficient methods for importing materialized view updates in real-time databases, analyzing update properties and comparing four scheduling algorithms to balance freshness and transaction timeliness, relevant to the conference topic H.2 (Database Management).
The paper proposes a microeconomics-inspired resource allocation framework for multi-query workloads, focusing on minimizing slowdown and ensuring fairness, relevant to the database systems field (H.2).
The paper introduces hypergraph abstraction and algorithms for optimizing complex queries with outer joins and duplicates, enabling cost reduction without exponential intermediate joins, relevant to conference topic H.2.
The paper introduces the Eager Compensating Algorithm (ECA) to eliminate anomalies in warehouse view maintenance caused by decoupled data sources, along with optimized variants and a performance comparison. Relevant conference: H.2.
The paper investigates efficient materialization and maintenance of mediated views across heterogeneous data sources, proposing improved algorithms for handling updates, including a novel fixpoint operator \( W_P \). Relevant to database systems (H.2).
The paper presents a simulation study of a scalable video-on-demand system, comparing advanced disk scheduling, prefetching, and buffer management algorithms against simpler approaches and demonstrating near-linear scalability with increasing resources. Relevant conference: H.5.
The paper proposes COPS, a system for detecting document copies in digital libraries, with algorithms and experimental results, presented in conference H.2.
The paper introduces the *Enterprise Objects Framework*, a tool integrating object-oriented programming with relational databases for business application development, presented in conference H.2.
The paper discusses advancements in storage technology, including increased areal density, higher data rates, RAID adoption, and the need for parallel storage systems, relevant to the conference topic H.2 (Database Management).
QBI is an icon-based query interface for distributed databases, simplifying query formulation without schema knowledge, relevant to conference topic H.2 (Database Management).
The paper discusses challenges in managing heterogeneous information in organizations, leading to "write-only" databases, with relevance to database systems (H.2).
The VisDB system, developed at the University of Munich, leverages human visual perception for interactive visualizations of large databases, related to conference topic H.2.

The paper describes a toolkit for combinatorial pattern matching and discovery in sequences and trees, with applications in molecular biology and document comparison, presented in the H.2 conference.
The paper proposes efficient algorithms for mining association rules between numeric and Boolean attributes, optimizing gain, support, or confidence, with a visualization system. It is related to the conference topic 'H.2' (Database Management).
The paper presents a client-server solution for business data analysis, integrating exploration and analysis tasks with a history mechanism, reusable graphical representations, and database capabilities, relevant to the H.2 conference.
The paper presents fault-tolerant approaches with data placement and admission control algorithms for continuous media servers, ensuring guaranteed retrieval rates during disk failures while maximizing client support, relevant to conference topic D.4.
The paper proposes methods for optimizing queries in multimedia repositories with multiple attribute types by minimizing index searches and efficiently handling independent predicates, extending traditional filtering to include ranking and top-k retrieval. Relevant conference: H.2.
The paper introduces **BIRCH**, an efficient clustering algorithm for large datasets that minimizes I/O costs, handles noise effectively, and achieves high-quality clustering with minimal scans, outperforming existing methods like CLARANS. Published in conference category H.3.
The paper presents an efficient online reorganization method for sparsely-populated B+-trees, involving leaf compaction, optional reordering, upper-tree shrinking, minimal locking, forward recovery, and a heuristic to reduce swaps while ensuring consistency and concurrency. Conference: E.1 (Data Structures).
The paper proposes a cost-based query optimization technique for mediator systems, leveraging cached statistics and semantic invariants to enhance performance, particularly in handling remote source challenges, as discussed in the H.2 conference.
The paper introduces **OLE DB**, a Microsoft-developed set of extensible COM-based interfaces enabling uniform, transactional access to diverse data sources (both DBMS and non-DBMS) by modularizing core database functionalities like query processing, transactions, and schema management. Relevant to database systems (H.2).
The paper discusses transactional replication instability under scaling workloads, proposes a two-tier replication algorithm with commutative updates to address deadlocks, and highlights master-copy replication advantages, relevant to database systems (H.2).
The paper proposes "hot mirroring," a storage management scheme for disk arrays that partitions space into high-performance mirrored regions for hot data and high-efficiency RAID5 regions for cold data, optimizing performance and minimizing rebuild degradation. Relevant conference: D.4 (Systems).
The paper proposes greedy algorithms for optimal view selection in data cubes, demonstrating near-optimal performance and tradeoff analysis in hypercube lattices, with relevance to conference category H.4.
The paper proposes **Q2P**, a quantified query processor using multidimensional and boolean matrix structures, to efficiently handle complex quantified queries in relational databases, demonstrating significant performance improvements for decision support applications. Conference: H.4.
The paper introduces a functional-based query language for multidimensional arrays, treating them as functions from indices to values, and presents its calculus, implementation, optimization rules, and expressiveness analysis. Relevant conference: H.2.
The paper introduces a spatial hash-join framework that outperforms tree-based spatial join methods, leveraging dynamic partition functions for the inner dataset and an immutable, replicating partition function for the outer dataset, eliminating the need for pre-computed indices. Relevant conference: H.2.
Paper on Bifocal sampling, a novel join size estimation technique, presented at conference H.2, with methods for sparse/dense tuple classification and accurate estimation using \( O(\sqrt{n} \log n) \) sampling.
The paper presents a comprehensive taxonomy of histograms for database systems, introduces new types and construction methods, and identifies the most effective histogram types for selectivity estimation through empirical evaluation. Relevant conference: H.2 (Database Systems).
The paper proposes an abstract-object storage model to uniformly manage internal and external data, leveraging database services like indexing and query processing, with geospatial metadata as an example, relevant to conference topic H.2.
The paper introduces *Class Fencing*, a goal-oriented buffer allocation algorithm based on *hit rate concavity*, improving responsiveness, robustness, and simplicity while maintaining accuracy for multi-class workloads. Relevant to conference category: H.2.
The paper surveys object placement algorithms for database systems, introduces a new algorithm for the Shore database system that outperforms current methods in CPU, memory, I/O, and disk utilization, and validates its effectiveness through experiments. Relevant conference: D.4.

Relevant conference: H.2 (Database Management).

The paper proposes Weighted Margin SVM (WMSVM), a generalization of SVM that incorporates prior knowledge to improve performance, demonstrating its effectiveness through experiments and showing compatibility with Sequential Minimal Optimization for training. Conference: I.5
The paper proposes the TAPER algorithm for efficient identification of strongly correlated item pairs in large datasets, leveraging a computationally cheaper upper bound of Pearson's correlation coefficient with pruning properties. It significantly reduces computation time compared to brute-force methods, presented in the H.2 conference.
The paper proves that counting distinct maximal frequent itemsets and patterns in sequences, trees, and graphs is #P-complete or #P-hard, presented in conference F.2.
The paper introduces Generalized Principal Component Analysis (GPCA), a dimension reduction method for image compression and retrieval that outperforms PCA by preserving spatial locality and improving efficiency in storage, query precision, and computational cost. Published in conference category H.3.
The paper proposes IDR/QR, an incremental dimension reduction algorithm using QR decomposition for LDA, offering lower computational cost and memory efficiency while maintaining competitive classification accuracy. Relevant conference: H.2.
The paper presents a statistical method for discovering significant statistical quantitative rules (SQ rules) using resampling techniques, addresses false discovery rates, and demonstrates its application on consumer purchase data. Relevant conference: H.2.
The paper proposes an efficient spatial join-based method for mining spatial collocation patterns, integrating neighborhood discovery with pattern mining, achieving significant performance gains over previous approaches. Relevant conference: H.2.
The paper describes TiVo's scalable, distributed item-item collaborative filtering system for TV show recommendations, leveraging client-side processing for efficiency. Context: Conference field I.2 (Artificial Intelligence).
The paper presents a prototype using individual customer classifiers trained on historical transaction data to predict shopping lists, improving retail revenues by up to 11% and enhancing customer experience. Relevant conference: H.2.
The paper proposes a rank sum test method for informative gene discovery, avoiding normality assumptions, with superior accuracy (96.2% on colon data, 100% on leukemia data). Presented at conference H.2.
The paper proposes using data mining techniques (decision trees, logistic regression, neural networks) to detect insider trading in option markets pre-news release, comparing performance against an expert model. Relevant conference: H.2 (Database Management).
The paper proposes two efficient algorithms, Sample-Gene Search and Gene-Sample Search, to mine coherent gene clusters from gene-sample-time microarray data, identifying phenotype-related samples and correlated genes. It is published in conference H.2.
The paper presents an eigenspace-based method for automated anomaly detection in multi-tier web systems, modeled as weighted graphs, with feature extraction from adjacency matrices and adaptive online thresholding for fault detection, related to conference category I.2 (Artificial Intelligence).
The paper proposes a localized clustering-regression method for efficient and accurate damage detection in large mechanical structures, presented at conference H.2, outperforming global models and previous hierarchical approaches in accuracy and computational efficiency.
The paper introduces **VizTree**, a novel visualization tool for mining and monitoring time-series data, particularly for aerospace telemetry, by transforming data into symbolic representations and displaying patterns in a modified suffix tree with visual encodings. The paper is associated with the conference topic [H.3].
The paper presents a machine learning-based approach for detecting malicious executables using n-gram bytecode features, with boosted decision trees achieving high accuracy (AUC 0.996) on a dataset of 1,971 benign and 1,651 malicious samples. Published in conference category H.2.
The paper proposes a novel algorithm that directly optimizes the concordance index (CI) via a differentiable approximation to improve prostate cancer recurrence prediction, outperforming traditional Cox models and other machine learning methods. Conference: H.2
The paper proposes a density-based spam detection method using document space density information, achieving 98% recall and 100% precision with unsupervised learning and handling over 13,000 emails per second, as validated by experiments on 50 million real emails. Relevant conference: H.2.
The paper introduces *V-Miner*, a tool that enhances parallel coordinate visualization by automatically rearranging variables using edit-distance techniques to reveal correlations in product design and test data, with case studies from Motorola. Relevant conference: H.2.
The paper proposes an on-demand classification model for evolving data streams, dynamically selecting training windows to adapt to changing data patterns, maintaining high accuracy efficiently. Relevant conference: H.2.
The paper presents a generalized Bregman divergence-based co-clustering framework, extending information-theoretic co-clustering to arbitrary matrices, introducing the minimum Bregman information principle, and providing a meta-algorithm for local optimality, unifying existing clustering methods. Conference: I.2.
The paper proposes an objective clustering evaluation criterion based on semi-supervised classification performance, quantified using the PAC-MDL bound, and demonstrates its effectiveness on text datasets, related to conference topic I.5.
The paper proposes a column-generation boosting method for classification and regression, using 1-norm or 2-norm regularization to select and combine kernels from a library, resulting in sparse, efficient models with improved testing speed. The work is related to the conference topic 'I.5' (Pattern Recognition and Machine Learning).
The paper introduces **IncSpan**, an efficient algorithm for incremental mining of sequential patterns in large, dynamically updated databases, leveraging key properties to avoid reprocessing the entire dataset. It is associated with the conference topic [H.2].
This paper presents parallel algorithms for computing high-dimensional robust correlation and covariance matrices (QC and Maronna methods), demonstrating their scalability and performance on large datasets, with QC being faster for small parallel systems and Maronna preferred for high robustness or large-scale parallel platforms. The research is relevant to the H.2 database systems field.
The paper proposes a POMDP-based approach for signaling alarms in surveillance systems, demonstrating its effectiveness over thresholding and CUSUM methods in handling single-output and spatio-temporal data using scan statistics. Conference: I.2
The paper proposes a steganalysis method to locate hidden messages in images by identifying outlier pixels based on energy measures, achieving 87% accuracy in color images and 61% in grayscale images among the top 0.33% of detected outliers. Conference: I.5
The paper establishes a theoretical connection between kernel \( k \)-means and spectral clustering, showing that normalized cut objectives can be optimized via weighted kernel \( k \)-means, enabling more efficient and flexible clustering algorithms. Conference: H.3
The paper introduces **Customer-Oriented Catalog Segmentation**, a problem where catalogs are designed to maximize customer interest, proposing efficient greedy and randomized algorithms. It is associated with the conference category [H.2].
The paper introduces *k-privacy*, a novel privacy model for large-scale distributed environments, generalizing the trusted third party approach to enable efficient and cryptographically secure multiparty computation, demonstrated through an association-rule mining application in Data Grids. Relevant conference: H.2.
The paper introduces a tree-based statistical method to detect extrapolation by distinguishing whether a point originates from the data distribution or a uniform null distribution, using modified CART for improved classification. Conference: G.3.
The paper proposes a method to quantify the importance of non-additive interactions in black box functions by projecting them onto additive models, enabling interpretability through graphical displays and parametric modeling of low-dimensional components. Relevant conference: I.5.
The paper proposes SPIN, an efficient algorithm for mining maximal frequent subgraphs from graph databases, presented at conference H.2. It extracts frequent trees first, then reconstructs maximal subgraphs, reducing output size and improving speed.
The paper extends spatial scan statistics by introducing flexible square pyramid shapes to detect and model growing and shifting space-time clusters, validated on brain cancer data. Conference: H.2
The paper demonstrates that collective inference reduces classification error in relational data by leveraging interdependencies among related instances, with effectiveness depending on specific model conditions. Relevant conference category: I.5.
The paper proposes a framework and metrics to assess privacy violations in data mining results, addressing concerns beyond input data confidentiality, related to conference topic H.2 (Database Management).
The paper proposes a lexicon randomization technique to enhance the robustness of signature-based near-replica detection, significantly improving recall by 40-60% with minimal computational overhead compared to traditional I-Match. Relevant conference: H.2.
The paper proposes algorithms to learn spatially variant dissimilarity measures from data, improving clustering stability and accuracy on textual datasets compared to existing methods. Conference: H.2
The paper proposes an efficient micro-clustering approach for tracking moving objects and identifying spatial-temporal patterns, outperforming K-Means in runtime, with relevance to the conference topic H.2 (Database Management).
The paper proposes an ontology-driven subspace clustering framework integrating hierarchical domain knowledge to enhance efficiency and interpretability, validated on gene expression data using gene ontology. Relevant conference: H.2.
The paper introduces the IOC algorithm, an efficient variant of k-nearest neighbor classification for high-dimensional, many-class datasets, which prunes non-majority classes early to achieve significant speedups over traditional methods. Relevant conference: I.2.
The paper proposes a polynomial-time Monte-Carlo algorithm for identifying biologically meaningful coClusters in gene expression data, where genes and samples follow a regulatory model with bounded relative error (sleeve-width), ensuring near-optimal results with high probability. Relevant conference: H.2.
The paper proposes using semantic concept detection to map video clips into semantic spaces via model vectors, enabling improved retrieval, classification, visualization, and data mining of multimedia content, with relevance to conference topic H.3.
The paper introduces the **Gaston** algorithm, which implements the "quickstart principle" to efficiently mine frequent substructures (paths, trees, and cyclic graphs) by progressively increasing complexity, and evaluates two frequency computation methods. The work is associated with the conference subject area [H.2].
The paper proposes "MMG," a scalable, graph-based method for automatically discovering cross-modal correlations in multimedia collections, which outperforms existing methods in auto-captioning accuracy on the Corel image database by up to 10 percentage points. Published in conference H.2.

The paper presents a distributed computation algorithm for exact linear regression analysis on vertically partitioned data without disclosing individual attribute values, enabling privacy-preserving collaborative modeling. Relevant conference: H.2.
The paper introduces *dense itemsets*, a generalization of frequent itemsets that allows for noise by requiring only a sufficiently dense submatrix of attributes, presents efficient algorithms for mining them (including top-*k* variants), and demonstrates their utility in data summarization and exploration. Conference: H.2
The paper proposes a framework for generalizing the notion of support in association analysis by decomposing it into two functions—one evaluating pattern strength per object and another summarizing these evaluations—and demonstrates its applicability to non-binary data and diverse pattern types, presented in the H.2 conference.

Conference: H.2
